Point counts were placed 250 meters between them. 10 minutes were expended on each point count. But the main technique was fixed distance transect (50 meters from the line at both directions). I cannot provided more information about methodology. I rest 2 hours for the lunch. URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS89975020	2016-08-11 09:19:27	10525	species	Chestnut Piculet	Picumnus cinnamomeus			1					Venezuela	VE	Zulia	VE-V							Municipio Cabimas, c. 10 km SE Cabimas, Cerro Rudal and vicinity	L888745	P	10.3581514	-71.3671875	2010-04-17	07:00:00	obsr54638	S6287604	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	180	1.500		4	1		0	1	0			This was a relatively small bird yet for a piculet it seemed large.  The bill appeared particularly large to me in that I think it would have extended at least as far back on the head as the rear edge of the auriculars, if not further.  Typical of a piculet, this bird's bill tapered from a moderately heavy base to a sharply pointed tip along a straight culmen that, when combined with the straight lower mandible, made the bill appear wedge-shaped overall.  This bird had a relatively large head with a moderately steep forehead and a conspicuously rounded crown and nape.  The body was plump and overall the bird had a somewhat hunch-backed appearance, with the posture maybe a little more horizontal than diagonal, and the tail held downward almost vertically.  The wings were short and rounded, with a primary projection that was no more than a sixth the length of the exposed secondaries, and wingtips that reached right about to the tips of the uppertail coverts.  The tail was maybe as long as the body without the head but it seemed to be a little shorter; it was relatively narrow, parallel-sided (if not tapered inward slightly), and rounded at the tip.  The legs were moderately long and stout, and the feet were quite large.--This bird had unusual plumage patterns for a piculet.  The forehead had a wedge-shaped mark of creamy-whitish that appeared to extend from the base of the upper mandible back to its junction with the crown, behind which the crown itself was black, maybe with a few tiny whitish dots.  The forehead patch did not appear to extend down into the lores but it may have included the supraloral region, given that it seemed to end right at the top, front edge of the eye (or at least at the orbital ring).  Behind the eye, the auricular and superciliary regions were the same deep rufous-chestnut color as the nape, back of the neck, back, and scapulars, all of which were uniform in appearance and coloration.  I never really saw the secondary coverts but the primary coverts appeared as a dusky wedge along the leading edge of the wing.  The remiges were also blackish but they had relatively broad fringes of an odd, pale brownish-gray, if not grayish-buff, that extended down the outer edges and, at least on the secondaries, across the tips of the feathers.  These fringes were narrowest right at the feather shaft, where they were nearly broken by the dark center of the feather, which was pointed distally.  It also appeared that the edges on the inner secondaries were a little paler than those on the other remiges, but the contrast was subtle.  The exposed primary tips were dusky brown and unmarked.  The tail had a relatively broad and well-defined stripe of creamy-whitish running right down the center.  On either side of this stripe was a back band that was not quite as broad, and then a narrow, white stripe, but I was unsure if the outer edges of the tail were again black.  Given that I saw this bird primarily from the back, my views of the upperparts were better than those of the underparts.  That said, the throat, breast, sides, flanks, and I think at least most of the belly, were the same deep rufous-chestnut color as the upperparts and they seemed as evenly colored.  I never did see the undertail coverts, the underside of the tail, or probably even the lower belly.--As noted above, this bird's bill was at least partially blocked, so I was unable to see its base.  What I did see of the distal part of the bill appeared quite blackish when seen under somewhat backlit conditions.  The eyes were clearly dark, possibly dark brown, but I had a difficult time being sure.  Surrounding the eye was what appeared to be a narrow orbital-ring that was blackish in coloration.  The legs and feet appeared quite blackish, at least in the light conditions under which I observed this bird.
